<div id="review_2596140300" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2596140300" />
    <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword"><img alt="Iryna *Book and Sword*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547595130p2/57236678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2596140300?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iryna *Book and Sword*" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword">Iryna *Book and Sword*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2596140300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12730141074560225672"><b>
  <u>*I got my husband to read this, and he in turn got his co-worker to read it. I believe I'm finally doing good in the world. </u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>“Let's not forget The Things They Do To Make Themselves Happy That Actually Make Them Miserable. This is an infinite list. It includes - shopping, watching TV, taking the better job, getting the bigger house, writing a semi-autobiographical novel, educating their young, making their skin look mildly less old and harboring a vague desire to believe there might be a meani</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12730141074560225672" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>*I got my husband to read this, and he in turn got his co-worker to read it. I believe I'm finally doing good in the world. </u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>“Let's not forget The Things They Do To Make Themselves Happy That Actually Make Them Miserable. This is an infinite list. It includes - shopping, watching TV, taking the better job, getting the bigger house, writing a semi-autobiographical novel, educating their young, making their skin look mildly less old and harboring a vague desire to believe there might be a meaning to it all.”</b><br /><br />If I was into highlighting my fiction books this WHOLE book would be highlighted. So much good stuff in it. It's really quite unfair that Matt Haig alone has gotten all of the world's wisdom, but at least he's sharing it with us, so that's good. Also, to clarify, I only rated this 4 and not 5 stars because there were some musings I didn't agree with, but for the most part I loved everything about this novel. <br /><br /><b>The Humans</b> is not a book that should be read for the plot. Yes, it's sci-fi, but it's not anything new, or groundbreaking, the plot is very recyclable and very, very predictable.<b> The Humans</b> is a book that should be read for its soul, for its wisdom and for the beauty that it finds in the mundane. Mundane meaning us - humans. And our meagre lives. <br /><br /><b>"But know this. Men are not from Mars. Women are not from Venus. Do not fall for categories. Everyone is everything. Every ingredient inside a star is inside you, and every personality that ever existed competes in the theatre of your mind for the main role."</b><br /><br />I realize that my review will consist mostly of quotes, but honestly with a book like this - it speaks for itself. I am merely a spectator, who was lucky enough to experience the masterpiece of this. And the beauty of this book is in how it unfolds itself.<br /><br />An unnamed alien comes to earth to take a place of a mathematician who solved a theorem that would have sped up the technological progress on earth to unfathomable levels, and aliens know that humans can't handle it, so they sent one of their own to exterminate the knowledge. The alien is repulsed by humans - he thinks us primitive, disgusting, and just backwards really. Are you offended yet? Because funnily enough, I agreed with every little thing he said about humans and all of our flaws. We, as species are truly horrible, and I finally have a book that wholeheartedly agrees with me. Feels good. <br /><br /><b>“Human life, I realized, got progressively worse as you got older, by the sound of things. You arrived, with baby feet and hands and infinite happiness, and then the happiness slowly evaporated as your feet and hands grew bigger. And then, from the teenage years onward, happiness was something you could lose your grip of, and once it started to slip, it gained mass. It was as if the knowledge that it could slip was the thing that made it more difficult to hold, no matter how big your feet and hands were.”<br /></b><br />But, as flawed as we are, there is something to us. And the alien goes on discovering what is it that makes humans so irresistible. Despite our feebleness, our single mindlessness and all our erroneous ways - humanity is real, it's raw, and it's painfully beautiful. I'm still not changing my opinions - I agree with alien's initial overview of human race, but I also agree that there's good in us, there's light and there's beauty - and all of that - the good and the bad is what makes us - the humans. <br /><br />The writing is superb, the humor is contagious - I highly recommend this, even to those who do not read sci-fi. This books is so much more than that. <br /><br /><b>“The tea seemed to be making things better. It was a hot drink made of leaves, used in times of crisis as a means of restoring normality.” </b><br /><br />My <a href="http://bookandsword.net " rel="nofollow noopener">WEBSITE</a><br />My <a href="https://www.instagram.com/book_and_sword/" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a><br />My <a href="https://bookandswordblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">WORDPRESS BLOG</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12730141074560225672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1665408540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1665408540" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1665408540?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1665408540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5677943032707476185">I absolutely loved the premise of this story so my expectation were sky high. Unfortunately that lead to a whole lot of disappointment on my part as this story turned out to be a distinctly average read. <br/><br/>The humor fell just a bit flat and I never really connected with any of the human characters on an emotional level. The alien host who stole Andrew Martin's body was actually the biggest success. He was suitably alien and I did enjoy how he grew to appreciate that humans had some good aspects as</span>
  <span id="freeText5677943032707476185" style="display:none">I absolutely loved the premise of this story so my expectation were sky high. Unfortunately that lead to a whole lot of disappointment on my part as this story turned out to be a distinctly average read. <br /><br />The humor fell just a bit flat and I never really connected with any of the human characters on an emotional level. The alien host who stole Andrew Martin's body was actually the biggest success. He was suitably alien and I did enjoy how he grew to appreciate that humans had some good aspects as well as the negative ones. The downside is that I could not care less about his romance with his wife or the rest of the humans we met along the way.<br /><br />The other disappointment was that the story had a slightly pretentious feel to it. Nothing strong enough to ruin the story, thankfully, but it was like an looming annoyance that lingered on the edges. <br /><br />Rating: 3 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: Mark Meadows did OK. He was a very English narrator and fit the very English feel of the story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5677943032707476185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3109768046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3109768046" />
    <a title="Aoife - Bookish_Babbling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22314328-aoife---bookish-babbling"><img alt="Aoife - Bookish_Babbling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554984281p2/22314328.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3109768046?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoife - Bookish_Babbling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoife - Bookish_Babbling" href="/user/show/22314328-aoife---bookish-babbling">Aoife - Bookish_Babbling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781786894663" href="/book/show/41135759-the-humans">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22314328-aoife---bookish-babbling?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22314328-aoife---bookish-babbling?shelf=bbf-book-borrowed-from-friend">bbf-book-borrowed-from-friend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3109768046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16997165200161795998">**this review might be a little spoiler'y for the opening pages of the book - but it is info we get immediately, so read on at your own risk. <br/>If you prefer going into books utterly blind...you've been warned 😎<br/><br/><i>Remember, during your mission, never become influenced or corrupted.<br/>The humans are an arrogant species, defined by violence and greed. They have taken their home planet, the only one they currently have access to, and placed it on the road to destruction. They have created a world of divisi</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16997165200161795998" style="display:none">**this review might be a little spoiler'y for the opening pages of the book - but it is info we get immediately, so read on at your own risk. <br />If you prefer going into books utterly blind...you've been warned 😎<br /><br /><i>Remember, during your mission, never become influenced or corrupted.<br />The humans are an arrogant species, defined by violence and greed. They have taken their home planet, the only one they currently have access to, and placed it on the road to destruction. They have created a world of divisions and categories and have continually failed to see the similarities between themselves.<br />They have developed technology at a rate too fast for human psychology to keep up with, and yet they still pursue advancement for advancement's sake, and for the pursuit of the money and fame they all crave so much.</i><br /><br />(While much of the above is true...I feel obliged to say #NotAllPeople 🤔)<br /><br /><br />This book is a humourous look at the human race from an outsider perspective. An Alien is sent to Earth to make sure the answer to a mathematical problem does not get released...by inhabiting the body of the individual who solved said equation. However the alien does not gain access to its hosts knowledge or memories and has to learn to adapt and blend in to achieve their mission. Which is immediately hilarious as the aliens baseline for learning the language system of Earth is reading Cosmo while standing starkers in a petrol station 😂🙈<br />This alien is a remarkably quick study, although to them, who revere mathematics, we are undoubtedly uncomplicated by comparison...However human interactions &amp; interpersonal connections puzzle them and so they observe and attempt to adapt with very entertaining fall out 👏<br /><br />There is such an innocence to them, despite their ultimately destructive goal...then there's Newton the dog who effectively changes everything because obvs animals are the shiz 😍🐶🤩<br />The original mathematicians family &amp; friends play really interesting roles in showing different facets of humanity and that despite what the alien governing authority that sent this boyo believes - not all humans are greedy destructive so-and-sos.<br /><br /><i>A paradox. The things you don't need to live - books, art, cinema, wine and so on - are the things you need to <b>live</b></i>.<br /><br />What a journey this alien goes on during the course of this book, and boy are we along for the ride as they learn about humanity. Newton &amp; Gulliver are my MVPs, such precious cinnamon rolls and should be protected at all costs. A special shout out for Winston Churchill also - unsurprisingly he leaves an impression 😉<br />I hit a bit of a roadblock as I neared the end when it got a little big-picture/philosophical/sci-fi'y...but then it corrected course and totes hit me upside the feels in such a way that my cold dark heart was warmed slightly &amp; I may have read that adorkably charming list with misty eyes and a small smile. 😅<br /><br />The chapter headings, if they can be called that, are fun tidbits and the chapters themselves are such short snapshots that they made one-more-chapter'itis possible, palatable &amp; for very addictive compulsive reading 👍<br />The list towards the end...that list destroyed me &amp; empowered me and generally just gave me all the sappy-happy feels! Had the book ended there with that list and a little more open ended this would have been closer to a 5* read for me. Probably still not 5 because of my other issues - but it deff would have been a smidge higher.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I have nothing against the more hopeful &amp; uplifting way this ended per se, but I don't feel it was necessary nor did it add anything to my enjoyment of the story. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The authors note at the end with the inspiration for this story was so poignant! I cannot imagine feeling that way and hope that in writing this it helped them and will hopefully help any and all who feel the same way at any point in their lives. Anxiety can affect any of us at any point and from what I understand, from close family members who sometimes feel these flutters...once that dam cracks, it can be hard to plug the drips and the memory of the anxious feelings never quite goes away but erodes our self-confidence and self-belief little by little like waves on a beach if left unchecked.<br /><br />Sci-fi is not a typical read for me, and tbh, I preferred the humour this book brought to the table. The more sci-fi elements got my back up and I think having experienced a similar knee-jerk reaction to certain themes in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2956954618?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sudden Appearance of Hope</a> last year. Perhaps it's time to admit defeat and that my initial reaction &amp; what I typically think when hearing most sci-fi books blurbed..."erm, no thanks - not for me", is probably my best course of action going forward.<br />I will continue to look more closely at humerous outlooks like this fun read, but I think ultimately they are all going to reach a point where the sci-fi questions-philosophical will be raised/addressed and I now realise they are just not my cup of tea...(Let's just pretend I actually drink tea - yes I know I'm a terrible excuse for an Irish person, but I digress 😉)<br /><br />This is all to say, I did very much enjoy this book and highly recommend it with the caveat that I deffo think I'm not cut out to be a sci-fi reader. So I cannot comment on those grounds, yet this book is still a very fun read for a layperson such as myself. Massive thanks to one of my kindly bookish work buddies who generously lent me this book back in the autumn (I think) last year - I promise to finally return this book and the others I've been lent hopefully at some point in 2020 🤗<br /><br />Solid 4* read as it did keep me smirking and giggling as they got to grips with our human ways</span>
  <a data-text-id="16997165200161795998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_610530636" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610530636" />
    <a title="Lou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3699303-lou"><img alt="Lou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312212794p2/3699303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/610530636?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lou" href="/user/show/3699303-lou">Lou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3699303-lou?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3699303-lou?shelf=other-beings">other-beings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer610530636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4873865994480679959"><b>Read my Interview with this author @ <a href='http://more2read.com/review/interview-with-matt-haig/' rel='nofollow noopener'>http://more2read.com/interview-with-matt-haig/</a> he chats on writing,his life,and an adaptation.</b><br/><br/>My Review<br/><br/>Humans,<br/>the divine comedy they represent,<br/>with all their delusions,<br/>with all their fictions,<br/>with all their religious beliefs,<br/>with all their sex, drugs and rock and roll,<br/>with all their technological advancement,<br/>with all their moral decline,<br/>with all their race and class differences,<br/>with all their love for money and fame,<br/>with all their lies and truths,<br/>with all the</span>
  <span id="freeText4873865994480679959" style="display:none"><b>Read my Interview with this author @ <a href="http://more2read.com/review/interview-with-matt-haig/" rel="nofollow noopener">http://more2read.com/interview-with-matt-haig/</a> he chats on writing,his life,and an adaptation.</b><br /><br />My Review<br /><br />Humans,<br />the divine comedy they represent,<br />with all their delusions,<br />with all their fictions,<br />with all their religious beliefs,<br />with all their sex, drugs and rock and roll,<br />with all their technological advancement,<br />with all their moral decline,<br />with all their race and class differences,<br />with all their love for money and fame,<br />with all their lies and truths,<br />with all their war and peace,<br />with all their sense and sensibility,<br />with all their sound and fury,<br />with all their to have and have not,<br />with all their disease and death,<br />And so they continue on beating against the cycle of time,<br />knowing all this, <br />against their allotted time of sparse existence,<br />they are a strange species, <br />they still carry on and keep calm despite this,<br />who in their right mind would want to be human?<br /><br />I read the Humans by author Matt Haig and his telling of one non-human beating against the tide of humanity in all its pot holes and weakness, I must warn fellow Vonnadorians who are reading this that this book is very dangerous and polluting to our species, the poetry recommended by the character in this story likewise, it may be infectious on the mind and the intellect of our species. I was quite magically taken under the writers wing and seeing this human world experience in first person and it all read to be quite credible. I must admit he fooled me with his narrative, he captivated me i was very keen on this humanity, taken in by this unique character of whom he has you have an empathic feeling for, but believe you me this is a farce. <br />Indeed even with all the weirdness and beauty of humanity portrayed in this story,<br />we do not need anything from humans, we have much more, we have immortality, what you have before you is a lasting and very brave accounting of the ins and outs, warnings of what it is like to be human, so that we may never want or try to be a human.<br /><br />My warning to Vonnadorians is.....<br />(Excerpt from The Humans by Matt Haig)<br />"Remember, during your mission, never to become influenced or corrupted.<br />The humans are an arrogant species, defined by violence and greed.<br />They have taken their home planet, the only one they currently have access to, and placed it on the road to destruction. They have created a world of divisions and categories and have continually failed to see the similarities between themselves. They have developed technology at a rate too fast for human psychology to keep up with, and yet they still pursue advancement for advancement's sake, and for the pursuit of the money and fame they all crave so much.<br />You must never fall into the humans trap. You must never look at an individual and fail to see their relation to the crimes of the whole, livery smiling human face hides the terrors they are all capable of and are all responsible for, however indirectly.<br />You must never soften, or shrink from your task.<br />Stay pure. <br />Retain your logic.<br />Do not let anyone interfere with the mathematical certainty of what needs to be done."<br /><br /><br /><b>May this book remain in our libraries as a stark warning on the frailty and art of being human.</b><br /><br /><br />Excerpt<br />"I was to be a married man. I was forty-three years old, the exact mid-point in a human life. I had a son. I was the professor who had just solved the most significant mathematic puzzle the humans had ever faced. I had, only three short hours ago, advanced the human race beyond anyone's imagining."<br /><br />My Review with a unique book trailer can be also viewed @ <a href="http://more2read.com/review/the-humans-by-matt-haig/" rel="nofollow noopener">http://more2read.com/review/the-humans-by-matt-haig/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4873865994480679959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('z4HtUSIVhdNM+ERc63qGCYeezON6wE2kgJQSL+SqOxS2x3/NFOGOaLemFH4LIRLebG8eEff8SK5xEuFOfWGyEQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ug1CX7GZs18P9mfkg8RRbMiYenxVgaXedrf816eMGdkrS9DDh2245PSoN8Zjn8W7I2mojti9oNSHMQ+2PkeQ3A==')})
  }
//]]>

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_1741139'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1741139.Prinzip_Menschlichkeit?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Prinzip Menschlichkeit<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/532492.Joachim_Bauer?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Joachim Bauer<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.81 avg rating &mdash; 31 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2008\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer16818995452251496254\">Ob das Wesen des Menschen von Natur auf Konflikt und Kampf oder aber auf mitmenschliche Kooperation angelegt ist, ist bis heute umstritten. Als Realist jedenfalls gilt gemeinhin derjenige, der die Auffassung vertritt, dass Kooperation eine Verhaltens<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16818995452251496254\" style=\"display:none\">Ob das Wesen des Menschen von Natur auf Konflikt und Kampf oder aber auf mitmenschliche Kooperation angelegt ist, ist bis heute umstritten. Als Realist jedenfalls gilt gemeinhin derjenige, der die Auffassung vertritt, dass Kooperation eine Verhaltensweise ist, die lediglich auf der den Menschen als Verstandeswesen auszeichnenden Einsicht beruht, dass man den ansonsten natürlichen Zustand des Kampfes aller gegen aller zum Wohle eines jeden Einzelnen und damit zugleich der Gemeinschaft überwinden und die in jedem Fall aber notwendige Konkurrenz zumindest regeln müsse. Das hört sich zwar einigermaßen vernünftig an, neuere Ergebnisse der neurobiologischen Forschung, über die Joachim Bauer in seinem Buch Prinzip Menschlichkeit berichtet, geben aber Grund zu der Annahme, dass die dieser Auffassung zugrunde liegenden Prämissen einer erneuten Prüfung unterzogen werden müssen. Gemäß der heute (noch) vorherrschenden Meinung gilt Konkurrenz als &quot;der biologische Antrieb des Lebens - auch des menschlichen&quot;: Da sich diese Auffassung &quot;nahtlos zum \'Kampf ums Überleben\' fügte, den Charles Darwin zur Grundregel der Natur erklärt hatte, schien für viele die Frage nach der Natur des Menschen geklärt&quot;, bringt Joachim Bauer zutreffend die Ursache für den von der Soziobiologie verordneten Diskussionsstillstand auf den Punkt. Unter Neurobiologen beginnt sich nun aber, wie der Autor ausführlich darlegt, die Erkenntnis durchzusetzen, dass das ursprüngliche Leitmotiv menschlichen Handelns eben nicht Konkurrenz ist, sondern ganz im Gegenteil Kooperation - in der Terminologie Joachim Bauers: das Prinzip Menschlichkeit: &quot;Kern aller menschlichen Motivation ist es, zwischenmenschliche Anerkennung, Wertschätzung, Zuwendung oder Zuneigung zu finden und zu geben.&quot; Das Konkurrenzmotiv wäre demnach eben nicht Ausdruck der primären Natur des Menschen, sondern im Gegenteil das Ergebnis einer Störung derselben! Eine sehr aufschlussreiche Lektüre, die Anlass gibt, viele längst für erledigt geglaubte Fragen neu zu diskutieren. In den Natur- wie den Sozialwissenschaften gleichermaßen. -- Andreas Vierecke<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"16818995452251496254\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16362192323435412845">Matt Haig was born in Sheffield, England in1975. He writes books for both adults and children, often blending the worlds of domestic reality and outright fantasy, with a quirky twist. His bestselling novels are translated into 28 languages. The Guardian has described his writing as 'delightfully weird' and the New York Times has called him 'a novelist of great talent' whose writing is 'funny, rive</span>
  <span id="freeText16362192323435412845" style="display:none">Matt Haig was born in Sheffield, England in1975. He writes books for both adults and children, often blending the worlds of domestic reality and outright fantasy, with a quirky twist. His bestselling novels are translated into 28 languages. The Guardian has described his writing as 'delightfully weird' and the New York Times has called him 'a novelist of great talent' whose writing is 'funny, riveting and heartbreaking'. <br /> <br />His novels for adults are The Last Family in England, narrated by a labrador and optioned for film by Brad Pitt; The Dead Fathers Club (2006), an update of Hamlet featuring an 11-year-old boy; The Possession of Mr Cave (2008), about a man obsessed with his daughter's safety, and The Radleys (2010) which won Channel 4's TV Book Club public vote and was shortlisted for a Galaxy National Book Award (UK). The film rights to all his adult novels have been sold. His next adult novel is The Humans (2013).<br /> <br />His multi-award winning popular first novel for children, Shadow Forest, was published in 2007 and its sequel, The Runaway Troll, in 2009. His most recent children's novel is To Be A Cat (2012).</span>
  <a data-text-id="16362192323435412845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

The earliest humans walked around naked with no problem. Certain humans, in humid rainforests mainly, still do so. So, we must conclude that madness is sometimes a question of time, and sometimes of postcode. <br /><br />Basically, the key rule is, if you want to appear sane on Earth you have to be in the right place, wearing the right clothes, saying the right things, and only stepping on the right kind of grass.&rdquo;</span>
